	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Bahá'í Faith</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#039;í">Bahá&#039;í</a>)</span></div>

<p>The <b>Bahá'í Faith</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span></span>, <wbr />-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">بهائی</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="fa-Latn" title="Persian-language romanization">Bahā'i</i></i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> teaching the essential worth of all religions, and the unity and equality of all people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDictionary2017_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDictionary2017-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (August 2019)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith#Dubious" title="Talk:Bahá&#39;í Faith">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> Established by <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá&#39;u&#39;lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a> in 1863, it initially grew in <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a> and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, where it has faced ongoing persecution since its inception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It is estimated to have between 5 and 8 million adherents, known as Bahá'ís, spread out into most of the world's countries and territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It grew from the mid-19th-century <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1bism" title="Bábism">Bábí religion</a>, whose founder (the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a>) taught that God would soon send a <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">prophet</a> in the same way of Jesus or Muhammad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEA.V.2017_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEA.V.2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 1863, after being banished from his native Iran, Bahá'u'lláh (1817–1892) announced that he was this prophet. He was further exiled, spending over a decade in the prison city of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Following Bahá'u'lláh's death in 1892, leadership of the religion fell to his son <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu&#39;l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a> (1844–1921), and later his great-grandson <a href="/wiki/Shoghi_Effendi" title="Shoghi Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</a> (1897–1957). Bahá'ís around the world annually elect local, regional, and national <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Assembly" title="Spiritual Assembly">Spiritual Assemblies</a> that govern the affairs of the religion, and every five years the members of all National Spiritual Assemblies elect the <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a>, the nine-member supreme governing institution of the worldwide Bahá'í community, which sits in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, Israel, near the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Shrine of the Báb">Shrine of the Báb</a>.
</p><p>Bahá'í teachings are in some ways similar to other monotheistic faiths: <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá&#39;í Faith">God</a> is considered single and all-powerful. However, Bahá'u'lláh taught that religion is orderly and progressively revealed by one God through <a href="/wiki/Manifestations_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifestations of God">Manifestations of God</a> who are the founders of <a href="/wiki/Major_world_religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Major world religions">major world religions</a> throughout history; <a href="/wiki/Buddha" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddha">Buddha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> being the most recent in the period before the Báb and Bahá'u'lláh. Bahá'ís regard the major religions as fundamentally unified in purpose, though varied in social practices and interpretations. There is a similar emphasis on the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of humanity">unity of all people</a>, openly rejecting notions of <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>. At the heart of Bahá'í teachings is the goal of a <a href="/wiki/New_world_order_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="New world order (Bahá&#39;í)">unified world order</a> that ensures the prosperity of all nations, races, creeds, and classes.<sup id="cite_ref-Hatcher_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hatcher-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Letters written by Bahá'u'lláh to various individuals, including some heads of state, have been collected and assembled into a canon of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá&#39;í literature">Bahá'í scripture</a> that includes works by his son <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu&#39;l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a>, and also <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">the Báb</a>, who is regarded as Bahá'u'lláh's forerunner. Prominent among Bahá'í literature are the <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-%C3%8Dq%C3%A1n" title="Kitáb-i-Íqán">Kitáb-i-Íqán</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Answered_Questions" title="Some Answered Questions">Some Answered Questions</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dawn-Breakers" title="The Dawn-Breakers">The Dawn-Breakers</a></i>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In English-language use, the word <i>Bahá'í </i> is used either as an adjective to refer to the Bahá'í Faith or as a term for a follower of Bahá'u'lláh. The word is not a noun meaning the religion as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman2006_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic language text"><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Name" class="mw-redirect" title="Greatest Name">Bahá‘</a></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">بهاء</span>), meaning "glory" or "splendor".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> The term "Bahaism" (or "Baha'ism") is still used, mainly in a pejorative sense,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998xiii_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998xiii-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECentre_for_Faith_and_the_Media_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentre_for_Faith_and_the_Media-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> though the U.S. Library of Congress uses "Bahaism" as a variant term for <i>Baha'i Faith</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs">Beliefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beliefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_teachings" title="Bahá&#39;í teachings">Bahá'í teachings</a></div>
<p>The teachings of Bahá'u'lláh, the founder of the Bahá'í Faith, form the foundation for Bahá'í belief.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  Three principles are central to these teachings: the <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá&#39;í Faith">unity of God</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of religion">unity of religion</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of humanity">unity of humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Baha'is believe that God periodically reveals his will through divine messengers, whose purpose is to transform the character of humankind and to develop, within those who respond, moral and spiritual qualities. Religion is thus seen as orderly, unified, and progressive from age to age.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008108–109_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008108–109-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="God">God</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: God">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá&#39;í Faith">God in the Bahá'í Faith</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A white domed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/170px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/255px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/340px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1662" data-file-height="2243" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bahá'í House of Worship in <a href="/wiki/Ingleside,_New_South_Wales" title="Ingleside, New South Wales">Ingleside</a>, Sydney, Australia</div></div></div>
<p>The Bahá'í writings describe a single, personal, inaccessible, omniscient, omnipresent, imperishable, and almighty God who is the creator of all things in the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008106_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008106-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Existence_of_God" title="Existence of God">existence of God</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> is thought to be eternal, without a beginning or end.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Though inaccessible directly, God is nevertheless seen as conscious of creation, with a will and purpose that is expressed through messengers termed <a href="/wiki/Manifestations_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifestations of God">Manifestations of God</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008106–107_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008106–107-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008111–112_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008111–112-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bahá'í teachings state that God is too great for humans to fully comprehend, or to create a complete and accurate image of by themselves. Therefore, human understanding of God is achieved through his revelations via his Manifestations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole19821–38_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole19821–38-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In the Bahá'í religion, God is often referred to by titles and attributes (for example, the All-Powerful, or the All-Loving), and there is a substantial emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>. The Bahá'í teachings state that the attributes which are applied to God are used to translate Godliness into human terms and also to help individuals concentrate on their own attributes in worshipping God to develop their potentialities on their spiritual path.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole19821–38_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole19821–38-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> According to the Bahá'í teachings the human purpose is to learn to know and love God through such methods as <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá&#39;í Faith">prayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Introspection" title="Introspection">reflection</a>, and being of service to others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051–38-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of religion">Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Progressive_revelation_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="Progressive revelation (Bahá&#39;í)">Progressive revelation (Bahá'í)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilmette_how_side.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white column with ornate designs carved into it, including a Star of David" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/170px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/255px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/340px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg 2x" data-file-width="967" data-file-height="1317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilmette_how_side.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Symbols of many religions on a pillar of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship_(Wilmette,_Illinois)" title="Bahá&#39;í House of Worship (Wilmette, Illinois)">Bahá'í House of Worship</a> in Wilmette, Illinois, U.S.</div></div></div>
<p>Bahá'í notions of progressive religious revelation result in their accepting the validity of the well known religions of the world, whose founders and central figures are seen as Manifestations of God. Religious history is interpreted as a series of <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">dispensations</a>, where each <i>manifestation</i> brings a somewhat broader and more advanced <a href="/wiki/Revelation" title="Revelation">revelation</a> that is rendered as a text of scripture and passed on through history with greater or lesser reliability but at least true in substance,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> suited for the time and place in which it was expressed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Specific religious social teachings (for example, the direction of prayer, or dietary restrictions) may be revoked by a subsequent manifestation so that a more appropriate requirement for the time and place may be established. Conversely, certain general principles (for example, neighbourliness, or charity) are seen to be universal and consistent. In Bahá'í belief, this process of progressive revelation will not end; it is, however, believed to be cyclical. Bahá'ís do not expect a new manifestation of God to appear within 1000 years of Bahá'u'lláh's revelation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen20007_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen20007-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bahá'í beliefs are sometimes described as <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> combinations of earlier religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman1997_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman1997-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'ís, however, assert that their religion is a distinct tradition with its own <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá&#39;í literature">scriptures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_teachings" title="Bahá&#39;í teachings">teachings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_laws" title="Bahá&#39;í laws">laws</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í history">history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBausani2012_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBausani2012-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> While the religion was initially seen as a sect of Islam, most religious specialists now see it as an independent religion, with its religious background in <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Shi&#39;a Islam">Shi'a Islam</a> being seen as analogous to the Jewish context in which Christianity was established.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Vyer1996449_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Vyer1996449-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  Muslim institutions and clergy, both <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a>, consider Bahá'ís to be deserters or <a href="/wiki/Apostasy_in_Islam" title="Apostasy in Islam">apostates from Islam</a>, which has led to Bahá'ís being <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá&#39;ís">persecuted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyleSheen1997119–120_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyleSheen1997119–120-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfshari2001119–120_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfshari2001119–120-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'ís describe their faith as an independent world religion, differing from the other traditions in its relative age and in the appropriateness of Bahá'u'lláh's teachings to the modern context.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELundberg2005_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELundberg2005-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'u'lláh is believed to have fulfilled the <a href="/wiki/Eschatology" title="Eschatology">messianic expectations</a> of these precursor faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuck2004143–178_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuck2004143–178-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_beings">Human beings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Human beings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of humanity">Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_on_life_after_death" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith on life after death">Bahá'í Faith on life after death</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringstone.svg" class="image"><img alt="A stylized Arabic figure which has intersecting lines that lock around rings and five-pointed stars to either side" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/220px-Ringstone.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/330px-Ringstone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/440px-Ringstone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringstone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_symbols#Ringstone_symbol" title="Bahá&#39;í symbols">ringstone symbol</a>, representing humanity's connection to God.</div></div></div>
<p>The Bahá'í writings state that human beings have a "rational <a href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a>", and that this provides the species with a unique capacity to recognize God's status and humanity's relationship with its creator. Every human is seen to have a duty to recognize God through his <a href="/wiki/Manifestation_of_God" title="Manifestation of God">messengers</a>, and to conform to their teachings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200057–58_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200057–58-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Through recognition and obedience, service to humanity and regular prayer and spiritual practice, the Bahá'í writings state that the soul becomes closer to God, the spiritual ideal in Bahá'í belief. According to Bahá'í belief when a human dies the soul is permanently separated from the body and carries on in the next world where it is judged based on the person's actions in the physical world. Heaven and Hell are taught to be spiritual states of nearness or distance from God that describe relationships in this world and the next, and not physical places of reward and punishment achieved after death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasumian1995_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasumian1995-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bahá'í writings emphasize the essential equality of human beings, and the abolition of prejudice. Humanity is seen as essentially one, though highly varied; its diversity of race and culture are seen as worthy of appreciation and acceptance. Doctrines of racism, nationalism, caste, social class, and gender-based hierarchy are seen as artificial impediments to unity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Bahá'í teachings state that the unification of humanity is the paramount issue in the religious and political conditions of the present world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><a href="/wiki/Shoghi_Effendi" title="Shoghi Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</a>, the head of the religion from 1921 to 1957, wrote the following summary of what he considered to be the distinguishing principles of Bahá'u'lláh's teachings, which, he said, together with the laws and ordinances of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a></i> constitute the bedrock of the Bahá'í Faith:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The independent search after truth, unfettered by <a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstition</a> or tradition; the oneness of the entire <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human race</a>, the pivotal principle and fundamental doctrine of the Faith; the basic unity of all religions; the condemnation of all forms of <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>, whether religious, racial, class or national; the harmony which must exist between religion and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_science" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and science">science</a>; the equality of men and women, the two wings on which the bird of human kind is able to soar; the introduction of compulsory education; the adoption of a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_auxiliary_language" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and auxiliary language">universal auxiliary language</a>; the abolition of the extremes of wealth and poverty; the institution of a <a href="/wiki/World_government" title="World government">world tribunal</a> for the adjudication of disputes between nations; the exaltation of work, performed in the spirit of service, to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a>; the glorification of justice as the ruling principle in human society, and of religion as a bulwark for the protection of all peoples and nations; and the establishment of a permanent and <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">universal peace</a> as the supreme goal of all mankind—these stand out as the essential elements [which Bahá'u'lláh proclaimed].<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEffendi1944281–282_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEffendi1944281–282-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_principles">Social principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Social principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following principles are frequently listed as a quick summary of the Bahá'í teachings. They are derived from transcripts of speeches given by <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu&#39;l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a> during his tour of Europe and North America in 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200852–53_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200852–53-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrinciples_of_the_Bahá&#39;í_Faith26_March_2006_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrinciples_of_the_Bahá&#39;í_Faith26_March_2006-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The list is not authoritative and a variety of such lists circulate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBausani2012_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBausani2012-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole1989438–446_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole1989438–446-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá&#39;í Faith">Unity of God</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of religion">Unity of religion</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and the unity of humanity">Unity of humanity</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_gender_equality" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and gender equality">Equality between women and men</a></li>
<li>Elimination of all forms of prejudice</li>
<li>World peace and a <a href="/wiki/New_world_order_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="New world order (Bahá&#39;í)">new world order</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_science" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and science">Harmony of religion and science</a></li>
<li>Independent investigation of truth</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_education" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and education">Universal compulsory education</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_auxiliary_language" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith and auxiliary language">Universal auxiliary language</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Obedience to government and non-involvement in partisan politics.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Elimination of extremes of wealth and poverty</li>
<li>Prohibition of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>.</li></ul>
<p>With specific regard to the pursuit of world peace, Bahá'u'lláh prescribed a world-embracing <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a> arrangement for the establishment of a temporary era of peace referred to in the Baha'i teachings as the Lesser Peace. For the establishment of a lasting peace (The Most Great Peace) and the purging of the "overwhelming Corruptions" it is necessary that all the people of the world universally unite under a universal Faith.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000266–267_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000266–267-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Covenant">Covenant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Covenant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Covenant of Bahá&#39;u&#39;lláh">Covenant of Bahá'u'lláh</a></div>
<p>The Bahá'í teachings speak of a "Greater Covenant",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1972_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1972-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> being universal and endless, and a "Lesser Covenant", being unique to each religious dispensation. The Lesser Covenant is viewed as an agreement between a Messenger of God and his followers and includes social practices and the continuation of authority in the religion. At this time Bahá'ís view Bahá'u'lláh's revelation as a binding lesser covenant for his followers; in the Bahá'í writings being firm in the covenant is considered a virtue to work toward.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1995_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1995-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Greater Covenant is viewed as a more enduring agreement between God and humanity, where a Manifestation of God is expected to come to humanity about every thousand years, at times of turmoil and uncertainty.
With unity as an essential teaching of the religion, Bahá'ís follow an <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_administration" title="Bahá&#39;í administration">administration</a> they believe is divinely ordained, and therefore see attempts to create schisms and divisions as efforts that are contrary to the teachings of Bahá'u'lláh. Schisms have occurred over the succession of authority, but any <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_divisions" title="Bahá&#39;í divisions">Bahá'í divisions</a> have had relatively little success and have failed to attract a sizeable following.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacEoin1989448_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacEoin1989448-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The followers of such divisions are regarded as <a href="/wiki/Covenant-breaker" title="Covenant-breaker">Covenant-breakers</a> and shunned, essentially <a href="/wiki/Excommunication" title="Excommunication">excommunicated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1995_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1995-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008173_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008173-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Canonical_texts">Canonical texts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Canonical texts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá&#39;í literature">Bahá'í literature</a></div>
<p>The <i>canonical texts</i> are the writings of the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a>, Bahá'u'lláh, `Abdu'l-Bahá, Shoghi Effendi and the <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a>, and the authenticated talks of `Abdu'l-Bahá. The writings of the Báb and Bahá'u'lláh are considered as divine revelation, the writings and talks of `Abdu'l-Bahá and the writings of Shoghi Effendi as authoritative interpretation, and those of the Universal House of Justice as authoritative legislation and elucidation. Some measure of divine guidance is assumed for all of these texts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000100–101_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000100–101-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Some of Bahá'u'lláh's most important writings include the Kitáb-i-Aqdas, literally the <i>Most Holy Book</i>, which defines many laws and practices for individuals and society,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin199846_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin199846-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-%C3%8Dq%C3%A1n" title="Kitáb-i-Íqán">Kitáb-i-Íqán</a>, literally the <i>Book of Certitude</i>, which became the foundation of much of Bahá'í belief,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998137_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998137-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Gems_of_Divine_Mysteries" title="Gems of Divine Mysteries">Gems of Divine Mysteries</a>, which includes further doctrinal foundations, and the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Valleys" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven Valleys">Seven Valleys</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Four_Valleys" title="The Four Valleys">the Four Valleys</a> which are mystical treatises.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200820_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200820-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mystical_writings">Mystical writings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mystical writings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although the Bahá'í teachings have a strong emphasis on social and ethical issues, a number of foundational texts have been described as mystical.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Seven_Valleys" title="The Seven Valleys">The Seven Valleys</a></i> is considered Bahá'u'lláh's "greatest mystical composition." It was written to a follower of <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>, in the style of <a href="/wiki/Attar_Neyshapuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Attar Neyshapuri">`Attar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persian</a> Muslim poet,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000311_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000311-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and sets forth the stages of the soul's journey towards God. It was first translated into English in 1906, becoming one of the earliest available books of Bahá'u'lláh to the West. <i><a href="/wiki/Hidden_Words" title="Hidden Words">The Hidden Words</a></i> is another book written by Bahá'u'lláh during the same period, containing 153 short passages in which Bahá'u'lláh claims to have taken the basic essence of certain spiritual truths and written them in brief form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000181_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000181-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table style="float:right; width:20%; border:1px solid #ddd; margin:0 0 1em 1em; padding:0 0 1em 1em; vertical-align:right; font-size:80%;">

<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="History of the Bahá&#39;í Faith">History of the Bahá'í Faith</a></div>
<p>The Bahá'í Faith formed from the Iranian religion of the Báb, a merchant who began preaching a new interpretation of Shia Islam in 1844. The Báb's claim to divine revelation was rejected by the generality of Islamic clergy in Iran, ending in his public execution by authorities in 1850. The Báb taught that God would soon send a new messenger, and Bahá'ís consider Bahá'u'lláh to be that person.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEA.V.2017_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEA.V.2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Although they are distinct movements, the Báb is so interwoven into Bahá'í theology and history that Bahá'ís celebrate his birth, death, and declaration as <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Holy_Days" title="Bahá&#39;í Holy Days">holy days</a>, consider him one of their three central figures (along with Bahá'u'lláh and `Abdu'l-Bahá), and a historical account of the Bábí movement (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Dawn-Breakers" title="The Dawn-Breakers">The Dawn-Breakers</a></i>) is considered one of three books that every Bahá'í should "master" and read "over and over again".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bahá'í community was mostly confined to the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Iranian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> empires until after the death of Bahá'u'lláh in 1892, at which time he had followers in 13 countries of Asia and Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1987125_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1987125-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Under the leadership of his son, `Abdu'l-Bahá, the religion gained a footing in Europe and America, and was consolidated in Iran, where it still suffers intense persecution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> After the death of `Abdu'l-Bahá in 1921, the leadership of the Bahá'í community entered a new phase, evolving from a single individual to an administrative order with both elected bodies and appointed individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200856_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200856-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_B.C3.A1b"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Báb">The Báb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Báb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A domed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/170px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/255px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/340px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Shrine of the Báb">Shrine of the Báb</a> in Haifa, Israel</div></div></div>
<p>On the evening of 22 May 1844, Siyyid `Alí-Muhammad of Shiraz gained his first convert and took on the title of "the Báb" (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">الباب</span> "the Gate"), referring to his later claim to the status of <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">Mahdi</a> of Shi`a Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> His followers were therefore known as <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1bism" title="Bábism">Bábís</a>. As the Báb's teachings spread, which the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_clergy" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic clergy">Islamic clergy</a> saw as a threat, his followers came under increased persecution and torture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The conflicts escalated in several places to military sieges by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of kings of Persia">Shah</a>'s army. The Báb himself was imprisoned and eventually executed in 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinter1997_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinter1997-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bahá'ís see the Báb as the forerunner of the Bahá'í Faith, because the Báb's writings introduced the concept of "<a href="/wiki/He_whom_God_shall_make_manifest" title="He whom God shall make manifest">He whom God shall make manifest</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Messianic_figure" class="mw-redirect" title="Messianic figure">Messianic figure</a> whose coming, according to Bahá'ís, was announced in the scriptures of all of the world's great religions, and whom Bahá'u'lláh, the founder of the Bahá'í Faith, claimed to be in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Báb's tomb, located in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa, Israel</a>, is an important place of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_pilgrimage" title="Bahá&#39;í pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> for Bahá'ís. The remains of the Báb were brought secretly from <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the Holy Land and eventually interred in the tomb built for them in a spot specifically designated by Bahá'u'lláh.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The main written works translated into English of the Báb's are collected in <a href="/wiki/Selections_from_the_Writings_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Selections from the Writings of the Báb">Selections from the Writings of the Báb</a> out of the estimated 135 works.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349–350_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349–350-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bah.C3.A1.27u.27ll.C3.A1h"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bahá&#039;u&#039;lláh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá&#39;u&#39;lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a></div>
<p>Mírzá Husayn `Alí Núrí was one of the early followers of the Báb, and later took the title of Bahá'u'lláh. Bábís faced a period of persecution that peaked in 1852–53 after a few individuals made a failed attempt to assassinate the <a href="/wiki/Naser_al-Din_Shah_Qajar" title="Naser al-Din Shah Qajar">Shah</a>. Although they acted alone, the government responded with <a href="/wiki/Collective_punishment" title="Collective punishment">collective punishment</a>, killing many Bábís. Bahá'u'lláh was put in prison. He claimed that in 1853, while incarcerated in the dungeon of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%ADy%C3%A1h-Ch%C3%A1l" title="Síyáh-Chál">Síyáh-Chál</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, he received the first intimations that he was the one anticipated by the Báb when he received a visit from the <a href="/wiki/Maid_of_Heaven" title="Maid of Heaven">Maid of Heaven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly thereafter he was expelled from Tehran to <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, in the Ottoman Empire;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> then to Constantinople (now <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>); and then to Adrianople (now <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>). In 1863, at the time of his banishment from Baghdad to Constantinople, Bahá'u'lláh declared his claim to a divine mission to his family and followers. Tensions then grew between him and <a href="/wiki/Subh-i-Azal" title="Subh-i-Azal">Subh-i-Azal</a>, the appointed leader of the Bábís who did not recognize Bahá'u'lláh's claim. Throughout the rest of his life Bahá'u'lláh gained the allegiance of most of the Bábís, who came to be known as Bahá'ís. Beginning in 1866, he began declaring his mission as a Messenger of God in letters to the world's religious and secular rulers, including <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>.
</p><p>He produced over 18,000 works in his lifetime, in both Arabic and Persian, of which only 8% have been translated into English.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bahá'u'lláh was banished by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BCl%C3%A2ziz" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdülâziz">Abdülâziz</a> a final time in 1868 to the Ottoman penal colony of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">`Akká</a>, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. Towards the end of his life, the strict and harsh confinement was gradually relaxed, and he was allowed to live in a home near `Akká, while still officially a prisoner of that city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole1989422–429_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole1989422–429-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> He died there in 1892. Bahá'ís regard his resting place at <a href="/wiki/Mansion_of_Bahj%C3%AD" title="Mansion of Bahjí">Bahjí</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Qiblih" title="Qiblih">Qiblih</a> to which they turn in prayer each day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200820–21,_28_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200820–21,_28-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id=".60Abdu.27l-Bah.C3.A1"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: `Abdu&#039;l-Bahá">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/220px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/330px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/440px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11049" data-file-height="12054" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>`Abdu'l-Bahá</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu&#39;l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a></div>
<p>`Abbás Effendi was Bahá'u'lláh's eldest son, known by the title of `Abdu'l-Bahá (Servant of Bahá). His father left a <a href="/wiki/Tablets_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h#Kitáb-i-`Ahd_(Book_of_the_Covenant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tablets of Bahá&#39;u&#39;lláh">will</a> that appointed `Abdu'l-Bahá as the leader of the Bahá'í community, and designated him as the "Centre of the Covenant", "Head of the Faith", and the sole authoritative interpreter of Bahá'u'lláh's writings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200847_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200847-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> `Abdu'l-Bahá had shared his father's long exile and imprisonment, which continued until `Abdu'l-Bahá's own release as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908. Following his release he led a life of travelling, speaking, teaching, and maintaining correspondence with communities of believers and individuals, expounding the principles of the Bahá'í Faith.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are over 27,000 extant documents by `Abdu'l-Bahá, mostly letters, of which only a fraction have been translated into English.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349–350_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349–350-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>  Among the more well known are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_of_Divine_Civilization" title="The Secret of Divine Civilization">The Secret of Divine Civilization</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Tablet_to_Dr._Forel" title="Tablet to Dr. Forel">Tablet to Auguste-Henri Forel</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Answered_Questions" title="Some Answered Questions">Some Answered Questions</a></i>. Additionally notes taken of a number of his talks were published in various volumes like <i><a href="/wiki/Paris_Talks" title="Paris Talks">Paris Talks</a></i> during his <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1%27s_journeys_to_the_West" title="`Abdu&#39;l-Bahá&#39;s journeys to the West">journeys to the West</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shoghi_Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Shoghi Effendi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shoghi_Effendi" title="Shoghi Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</a></div>
<p>Bahá'u'lláh's <i>Kitáb-i-Aqdas</i> and <i>The <a href="/wiki/Will_and_Testament_of_%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="Will and Testament of `Abdu&#39;l-Bahá">Will and Testament of `Abdu'l-Bahá</a></i> are foundational documents of the Bahá'í administrative order. Bahá'u'lláh established the elected <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a>, and `Abdu'l-Bahá established the appointed hereditary Guardianship and clarified the relationship between the two institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200855–57_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200855–57-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In his Will, `Abdu'l-Bahá appointed Shoghi Effendi, his eldest grandson, as the Guardian of the Bahá'í Faith.  Shoghi Effendi served for 36 years as the head of the religion until his death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200855_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200855-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shoghi Effendi throughout his lifetime translated <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_texts" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í texts">Bahá'í texts</a>; developed global plans for the expansion of the Bahá'í community; developed the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_World_Centre" title="Bahá&#39;í World Centre">Bahá'í World Centre</a>; carried on a voluminous correspondence with communities and individuals around the world; and built the administrative structure of the religion, preparing the community for the election of the Universal House of Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He unexpectedly died after a brief illness on 4 November 1957, in London, England, under conditions that did not allow for a successor to be appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh2000347–363_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh2000347–363-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200858–69_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200858–69-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1937, Shoghi Effendi launched a seven-year plan for the Bahá'ís of North America, followed by another in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaneshDaneshDanesh1991_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaneshDaneshDanesh1991-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 1953, he launched the first international plan, the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Year_Crusade" title="Ten Year Crusade">Ten Year World Crusade</a>. This plan included extremely ambitious goals for the expansion of Bahá'í communities and institutions, the translation of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_texts" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í texts">Bahá'í texts</a> into several new languages, and the sending of <a href="/wiki/Pioneering_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="Pioneering (Bahá&#39;í)">Bahá'í pioneers</a> into previously unreached nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHassal19961–21_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHassal19961–21-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He announced in letters during the Ten Year Crusade that it would be followed by other plans under the direction of the Universal House of Justice, which was elected in 1963 at the culmination of the Crusade. The House of Justice then launched a nine-year plan in 1964, and a series of subsequent multi-year plans of varying length and goals followed, guiding the direction of the international Bahá'í community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universal_House_of_Justice">Universal House of Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Universal House of Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willmette_how.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white domed building with a large garden leading toward it" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/220px-Willmette_how.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/330px-Willmette_how.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/440px-Willmette_how.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willmette_how.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship_(Wilmette,_Illinois)" title="Bahá&#39;í House of Worship (Wilmette, Illinois)">Bahá'í House of Worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilmette,_Illinois" title="Wilmette, Illinois">Wilmette, Illinois</a>, is the oldest surviving Bahai House of Worship in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan19876_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan19876-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Since 1963, the Universal House of Justice has been the elected head of the Bahá'í Faith. The general functions of this body are defined through the writings of Bahá'u'lláh and clarified in the writings of Abdu'l-Bahá and Shoghi Effendi. These functions include teaching and education, implementing Bahá'í laws, addressing social issues, and caring for the weak and the poor.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The House of Justice directs the work of the Bahá'í community through a series of multi-year international plans that began with a nine-year plan in 1964.  In the current plan, the House of Justice encourages the Bahá'ís around the world to focus on capacity building through children's classes, junior youth groups, devotional gatherings, and study circles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGervais2008_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGervais2008-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice17_January_2003_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice17_January_2003-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Additional lines of action include <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_development_and_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Socioeconomic development and the Bahá&#39;í Faith">social action</a> and participation in the prevalent discourses of society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVahedi2_March_2011_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVahedi2_March_2011-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice21_April_2010_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice21_April_2010-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The years from 2001 until 2021 represent four successive five-year plans, culminating in the centennial anniversary of the passing of `Abdu'l-Bahá.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_Of_Justice2006_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_Of_Justice2006-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>  Annually, on 21 April, the Universal House of Justice sends a ‘<a href="/wiki/Ridv%C3%A1n" title="Ridván">Ridván</a>’ message to the worldwide Bahá’í community,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000297_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000297-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> that updates Bahá'ís on current developments and provides further guidance for the year to come.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At local, regional, and national levels, Bahá'ís elect members to nine-person <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Assembly" title="Spiritual Assembly">Spiritual Assemblies</a>, which run the affairs of the religion. There are also <a href="/wiki/Institution_of_the_Counsellors" title="Institution of the Counsellors">appointed individuals</a> working at various levels, including locally and internationally, which perform the function of propagating the teachings and protecting the community. The latter do not serve as clergy, which the Bahá'í Faith does not have.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008160_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008160-77">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a> remains the supreme governing body of the Bahá'í Faith, and its 9 members are elected every five years by the members of all National Spiritual Assemblies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman1995_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman1995-78">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Any male Bahá'í, 21 years or older, is eligible to be elected to the Universal House of Justice; all other positions are open to male and female Bahá'ís.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008205_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008205-79">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_by_continent" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith by continent">Bahá'í Faith by continent</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_statistics" title="Bahá&#39;í statistics">Bahá'í statistics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large temple in the shape of an open lotus flower" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg/280px-Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg/420px-Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg/560px-Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5070" data-file-height="3380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotus_Temple_in_New_Delhi_03-2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Bahá&#39;í House of Worship">Bahá'í House of Worship</a> in New Delhi, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. It attracts an average of 4 million visitors a year.</div></div></div>
<p>A Bahá'í-published document reported 4.74 million Bahá'ís in 1986 growing at a rate of 4.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERabbaniJuly_19872–7_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabbaniJuly_19872–7-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'í sources since 1991 usually estimate the worldwide Bahá'í population to be above 5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service2010_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service2010-81">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/World_Christian_Encyclopedia" title="World Christian Encyclopedia">World Christian Encyclopedia</a></i> estimated 7.1 million Bahá'ís in the world in 2000, representing 218 countries,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrett20014_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrett20014-82">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and 7.3 million in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> with the same source. They further state: "The Baha'i Faith is the only religion to have grown faster in every United Nations region over the past 100 years than the general population; Baha’i was thus the fastest-growing religion between 1910 and 2010, growing at least twice as fast as the population of almost every UN region."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnsonGrim201359–62_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnsonGrim201359–62-84">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> This source's only systematic flaw was to consistently have a higher estimate of Christians than other cross-national data sets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHsuReynoldsHackettGibbon2008691–692_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuReynoldsHackettGibbon2008691–692-85">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bahá'í Faith is currently the largest religious minority in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Panama,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_174_2asp_National_Profile:_Panama&#93;_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_174_2asp_National_Profile:_Panama]-87">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Belize,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_23_2asp_National_Profile:_Belize&#93;_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_23_2asp_National_Profile:_Belize]-88">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and South Carolina;<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> the second largest international religion in Bolivia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_27_2asp_National_Profile:_Bolivia&#93;_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_27_2asp_National_Profile:_Bolivia]-90">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Zambia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_245_2asp_National_Profile:_Zambia&#93;_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_245_2asp_National_Profile:_Zambia]-91">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and Papua New Guinea;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_175_2asp_National_Profile:_Papua_New_Guinea&#93;_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_175_2asp_National_Profile:_Papua_New_Guinea]-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and the third largest international religion in Chad<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReligious_Intelligence_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReligious_Intelligence-93">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_45_2asp_National_Profile:_Chad&#93;_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacountriesCountry_45_2asp_National_Profile:_Chad]-94">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010&#91;httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacounitriesCountry_121_2asp_National_Profiles:_Kenya&#93;_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010[httpwwwtheardacominternationalDatacounitriesCountry_121_2asp_National_Profiles:_Kenya]-95">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/World_Almanac" title="World Almanac">The World Almanac and Book of Facts 2004</a></i>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The majority of Bahá'ís live in Asia (3.6 million), Africa (1.8 million), and Latin America (900,000). According to some estimates, the largest Bahá'í community in the world is in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, with 2.2 million Bahá'ís, next is <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, with 350,000, the US, with 150,000, and Brazil, with 60,000. Aside from these countries, numbers vary greatly. Currently, no country has a Bahá'í majority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPark2004_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPark2004-96">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The Bahá'í Faith is a medium-sized religion<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2008118_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2008118-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and was listed in <i>The Britannica Book of the Year</i> (1992–present) as the second most widespread of the world's independent religions in terms of the number of countries represented. According to <i>Britannica</i>, the Bahá'í Faith (as of 2010) is established in 221 countries and territories and has an estimated seven million adherents worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Bahá'ís have self-organized in most of the nations of the world.
</p><p>The Bahá'í religion was ranked by the Foreign Policy magazine as the world's second <a href="/wiki/Fastest_growing_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Fastest growing religion">fastest growing religion</a> by percentage (1.7%) in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForeign_Policy_Magazine1_May_2007_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForeign_Policy_Magazine1_May_2007-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_practices">Social practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Social practices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_laws" title="Bahá&#39;í laws">Bahá'í laws</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exhortations">Exhortations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Exhortations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following are a few examples from Bahá'u'lláh's teachings on personal conduct that are required or encouraged of his followers:
</p>
<ul><li>Bahá'ís over the age of 15 should individually recite an <a href="/wiki/Obligatory_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_prayers" title="Obligatory Bahá&#39;í prayers">obligatory prayer</a> each day, using fixed words and form.</li>
<li>In addition to the daily obligatory prayer, Bahá'ís should offer daily devotional prayer and to meditate and study sacred scripture.</li>
<li>Adult Bahá'ís should observe a <a href="/wiki/Nineteen-Day_Fast" title="Nineteen-Day Fast">Nineteen-Day Fast</a> each year during daylight hours in March, with certain exemptions.</li>
<li>There are specific requirements for Bahá'í burial that include a specified prayer to be read at the interment. Embalming or cremating the body is strongly discouraged.</li>
<li>Bahá'ís should make a 19% voluntary payment on any wealth in excess of what is necessary to live comfortably, after the remittance of any outstanding debt. These <a href="/wiki/Huq%C3%BAqu%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Huqúqu&#39;lláh">Huqúqu'lláh</a> payments are to be used for philanthropic purposes.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prohibitions">Prohibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Prohibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Elaborate gardens with several gates and a walkway leading to a domed building in the distance" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens" title="Bahá&#39;í gardens">Bahá'í gardens</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haifa,_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Haifa, Israel">Haifa, Israel</a></div></div></div>
<p>The following are a few examples from Bahá'u'lláh's teachings on personal conduct that are prohibited or discouraged.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Backbiting" title="Backbiting">Backbiting</a> and gossip are prohibited and denounced.</li>
<li>Drinking or selling <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a> is forbidden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">Sexual intercourse</a> is only permitted between a husband and wife, and thus premarital, extramarital, or homosexual intercourse are forbidden. <i>(See also <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_and_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Homosexuality and the Bahá&#39;í Faith">Homosexuality and the Bahá'í Faith</a>)</i></li>
<li>Abstaining from <a href="/wiki/Partisan_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Partisan (political)">partisan</a> politics is required.</li>
<li>Begging as a profession is forbidden.</li></ul>
<p>While some of the laws from the Kitáb-i-Aqdas are applicable at the present time, others are dependent upon the existence of a predominantly Bahá'í society, such as the punishments for arson or murder. The laws, when not in direct conflict with the civil laws of the country of residence, are binding on every Bahá'í,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008158_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008158-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and the observance of personal laws, such as prayer or fasting, is the sole responsibility of the individual.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000223–225_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000223–225-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalbridge1996_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalbridge1996-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_marriage" title="Bahá&#39;í marriage">Bahá'í marriage</a></div>
<p>The purpose of marriage in the Bahá'i faith is mainly to foster spiritual harmony, fellowship and unity between a man and a woman and to provide a stable and loving environment for the rearing of children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164–165_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164–165-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The Bahá'í teachings on marriage call it a <i>fortress for well-being and salvation</i> and place marriage and the family as the foundation of the structure of <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">human society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'u'lláh highly praised marriage, discouraged divorce, and required <a href="/wiki/Chastity" title="Chastity">chastity</a> outside of marriage; Bahá'u'lláh taught that a husband and wife should strive to improve the spiritual life of each other.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaha&#39;is_of_Warwick12_October_2003_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaha&#39;is_of_Warwick12_October_2003-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">Interracial marriage</a> is also highly praised throughout Bahá'í scripture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
