</p><p>Bahá'ís intending to marry are asked to obtain a thorough understanding of the other's character before deciding to marry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Although parents should not <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">choose partners for their children</a>, once two individuals decide to marry, they must receive the consent of all living biological parents, whether they are Bahá'í or not. The Bahá'í marriage ceremony is simple; the only compulsory part of the wedding is the reading of the wedding vows prescribed by Bahá'u'lláh which both the groom and the bride read, in the presence of two witnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The vows are "We will all, verily, abide by the Will of God."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008164_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008164-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work">Work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bahá'u'lláh prohibited a <a href="/wiki/Mendicancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Mendicancy">mendicant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">ascetic</a> lifestyle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008154–155_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008154–155-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">Monasticism</a> is forbidden, and Bahá'ís are taught to practice spirituality while engaging in useful work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The importance of self-exertion and service to humanity in one's spiritual life is emphasised further in Bahá'u'lláh's writings, where he states that work done in the spirit of service to humanity enjoys a rank equal to that of prayer and worship in the sight of God.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_worship">Places of worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Places of worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Bahá&#39;í House of Worship">Bahá'í House of Worship</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white domed building with palm trees in front of it" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg/220px-House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg/330px-House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg/440px-House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Worship_Germany_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bahá'í House of Worship, <a href="/wiki/Langenhain" title="Langenhain">Langenhain</a>, Germany</div></div></div>
<p>Most Bahá'í meetings occur in individuals' homes, local Bahá'í centers, or rented facilities. Worldwide, as of 2018, ten Bahá'í Houses of Worship, including eight Mother Temples and two local Houses of Worship have been built<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and a further five are planned for construction. Two of these houses of worship are national while the other three are going to be local temples.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'í writings refer to an institution called a "Ma<u>sh</u>riqu'l-A<u>dh</u>kár" (Dawning-place of the Mention of God), which is to form the center of a complex of institutions including a hospital, university, and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008194_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008194-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The first ever Ma<u>sh</u>riqu'l-A<u>dh</u>kár in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">`Ishqábád, Turkmenistan</a>, has been the most complete House of Worship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000236_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000236-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar">Calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_calendar" title="Bahá&#39;í calendar">Bahá'í calendar</a></div>
<p>The Bahá'í calendar is based upon the calendar established by the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a>. The year consists of 19 months, each having 19 days, with four or five <a href="/wiki/Ayy%C3%A1m-i-H%C3%A1" title="Ayyám-i-Há">intercalary days</a>, to make a full <a href="/wiki/Tropical_year" title="Tropical year">solar year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737–740-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Bahá'í New Year corresponds to the traditional Iranian New Year, called <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Naw-R%C3%BAz" title="Bahá&#39;í Naw-Rúz">Naw Rúz</a>, and occurs on the <a href="/wiki/Vernal_equinox" class="mw-redirect" title="Vernal equinox">vernal equinox</a>, near 21 March, at the end of the month of fasting. Bahá'í communities gather at the beginning of each month at a meeting called a <a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Day_Feast" title="Nineteen Day Feast">Feast</a> for worship, consultation and socializing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_17-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each of the 19 months is given a name which is an attribute of God; some examples include Bahá’ (Splendour), ‘Ilm (Knowledge), and Jamál (Beauty).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008188–190_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008188–190-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The Bahá'í week is familiar in that it consists of seven days, with each day of the week also named after an attribute of God. Bahá'ís observe 11 <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension of Bahá&#39;u&#39;lláh">Holy Days</a> throughout the year, with work suspended on 9 of these. These days commemorate important anniversaries in the history of the religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008188_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008188-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Arabic script inscribed on a metal plate" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg/280px-051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg/420px-051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg/560px-051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:051907_Wilmette_IMG_1404_The_Greatest_Name.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The calligraphy of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_symbols#The_Greatest_Name" title="Bahá&#39;í symbols">Greatest Name</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_symbols" title="Bahá&#39;í symbols">Bahá'í symbols</a></div><p>
The symbols of the religion are derived from the Arabic word Bahá’ (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">بهاء</span> "splendor" or "glory"), with a <a href="/wiki/Abjad_numerals" title="Abjad numerals">numerical value</a> of 9, which is why the most common symbol is the <a href="/wiki/Nine-pointed_star" class="mw-redirect" title="Nine-pointed star">nine-pointed star</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000167–168_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000167–168-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The ringstone symbol and calligraphy of the Greatest Name are also often encountered. The former consists of two five-pointed stars interspersed with a stylized Bahá’ whose shape is meant to recall the three onenesses,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaizi1968_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaizi1968-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> while the latter is a calligraphic rendering of the phrase Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">يا بهاء الأبهى</span> "O Glory of the Most Glorious!").</p><div style="clear:left;"></div><p>The five-pointed star is the official symbol of the Bahá'í Faith,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEffendi197351–52_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEffendi197351–52-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahai-library.comNine-Pointed_Star_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahai-library.comNine-Pointed_Star-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> known as the <i>Haykal</i> ("temple"). It was initiated and established by the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a> and various works were written in calligraphy shaped into a five-pointed star.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeyer2017_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeyer2017-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Socio-economic_development">Socio-economic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Socio-economic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Socio-economic_development_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economic development (Bahá&#39;í)">Socio-economic development (Bahá'í)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarbiyat_School,_Tehran,_ca_1911.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black-and-white photograph of several dozen girls seated in front of a school building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg/280px-Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg/420px-Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg/560px-Tarbiyat_School%2C_Tehran%2C_ca_1911.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2106" data-file-height="1573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarbiyat_School,_Tehran,_ca_1911.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students of <i>School for Girls</i>, <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, 13 August 1933. This photograph may be of the students of <i>Tarbiyat School for Girls</i> which was established by the Bahá'í Community of Tehran in 1911; the school was closed by government decree in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community2005_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community2005-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Since its inception the Bahá'í Faith has had involvement in <a href="/wiki/Socio-economic_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economic development">socio-economic development</a> beginning by giving greater freedom to women,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1994_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1994-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>  promulgating the promotion of female education as a priority concern,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKingdon1997_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKingdon1997-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and that involvement was given practical expression by creating schools, agricultural co-ops, and clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1994_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1994-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The religion entered a new phase of activity when a message of the Universal House of Justice dated 20 October 1983 was released. Bahá'ís were urged to seek out ways, compatible with the Bahá'í teachings, in which they could become involved in the social and economic development of the communities in which they lived. Worldwide in 1979 there were 129 officially recognized Bahá'í socio-economic development projects. By 1987, the number of officially recognized development projects had increased to 1482.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Current initiatives of social action include activities in areas like health, sanitation, education, gender equality, arts and media, agriculture, and the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá’í_Office_of_Social_and_Economic_Development2018_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá’í_Office_of_Social_and_Economic_Development2018-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Educational projects include schools, which range from village tutorial schools to large secondary schools, and some universities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen2007_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen2007-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> By 2017 there were an estimated 40,000 small scale projects, 1,400 sustained projects, and 135 Bahá'í inspired organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá’í_Office_of_Social_and_Economic_Development2018_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá’í_Office_of_Social_and_Economic_Development2018-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations">United Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: United Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bahá'u'lláh wrote of the need for <a href="/wiki/World_government" title="World government">world government</a> in this age of humanity's collective life. Because of this emphasis the international Bahá'í community has chosen to support efforts of improving <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> through organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, with some reservations about the present structure and constitution of the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen2007_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen2007-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_International_Community" title="Bahá&#39;í International Community">Bahá'í International Community</a> is an agency under the direction of the Universal House of Justice in Haifa, and has consultative status with the following organizations:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200039_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200039-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community6_June_2000_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community6_June_2000-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">United Nations Children's Fund</a> (UNICEF)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Fund_for_Women" title="United Nations Development Fund for Women">United Nations Development Fund for Women</a> (UNIFEM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">United Nations Economic and Social Council</a> (ECOSOC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO)</li></ul>
<p>The Bahá'í International Community has offices at the United Nations in New York and <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> and representations to United Nations regional commissions and other offices in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, Rome, <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community6_June_2000_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_International_Community6_June_2000-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, an Office of the Environment and an Office for the Advancement of Women were established as part of its United Nations Office. The Bahá'í Faith has also undertaken joint development programs with various other United Nations agencies. In the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Forum</a> of the United Nations a Bahá'í was invited as the only non-governmental speaker during the summit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service8_September_2000_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service8_September_2000-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Persecution">Persecution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Persecution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá&#39;ís">Persecution of Bahá'ís</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Broken cinder blocks and felled palm trees" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg/280px-Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg/420px-Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg/560px-Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cemetery_of_yazd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bahá'í cemetery in <a href="/wiki/Yazd" title="Yazd">Yazd</a> after its desecration by the Iranian government</div></div></div>
<p>Bahá'ís continue to be persecuted in Islamic countries, as Islamic leaders do not recognize the Bahá'í Faith as an independent religion, but rather as <a href="/wiki/Apostasy_from_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostasy from Islam">apostasy from Islam</a>. The most severe persecutions have occurred in <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Iran" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith in Iran">Iran</a>, where more than 200 Bahá'ís were executed between 1978 and 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Egypt" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith in Egypt">Egypt</a>. The rights of Bahá'ís have been restricted to greater or lesser extents in numerous other countries, including <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Afghanistan" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith in Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013&#91;https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222323_Afghanistan&#93;_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013[https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222323_Afghanistan]-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013&#91;https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222133_Indonesia&#93;_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013[https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222133_Indonesia]-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013&#91;https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222291_Iraq&#93;_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013[https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222291_Iraq]-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013&#91;https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222305_Morocco&#93;_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013[https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222305_Morocco]-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>  and several countries in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963–91-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The marginalization of the Iranian Bahá'ís by current governments is rooted in historical efforts by Muslim clergy to persecute the religious minority. When the Báb started attracting a large following, the clergy hoped to stop the movement from spreading by stating that its followers were enemies of God. These clerical directives led to mob attacks and public executions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Starting in the twentieth century, in addition to repression aimed at individual Bahá'ís, centrally directed campaigns that targeted the entire Bahá'í community and its institutions were initiated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In one case in Yazd in 1903 more than 100 Bahá'ís were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENash1982_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENash1982-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'í schools, such as the Tarbiyat boys' and girls' schools in Tehran, were closed in the 1930s and 1940s, Bahá'í marriages were not recognized and Bahá'í texts were censored.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanasarian200052–53_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanasarian200052–53-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a>, to divert attention from economic difficulties in Iran and from a growing nationalist movement, a campaign of persecution against the Bahá'ís was instituted.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;note 5&#93;</a></sup> An approved and coordinated anti-Bahá'í campaign (to incite public passion against the Bahá'ís) started in 1955 and it included the spreading of anti-Bahá'í propaganda on national radio stations and in official newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> During that campaign, initiated by Mulla Muhammad Taghi Falsafi,  the Baha'i center in Tehran was demolished at the orders of Tehran military governor, General Timor Bakhtiar.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1970s the Shah's regime consistently lost legitimacy due to criticism that it was pro-Western. As the anti-Shah movement gained ground and support, revolutionary propaganda was spread which alleged that some of the Shah's advisors were Bahá'ís.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbrahamian1982432_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbrahamian1982432-135">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'ís were portrayed as economic threats, and as supporters of Israel and the West, and societal hostility against the Bahá'ís increased.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpsonShubart1995223_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpsonShubart1995223-136">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Islamic Revolution</a> of 1979 Iranian <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Bahá'ís</a> have regularly had their homes ransacked or have been banned from attending university or from holding government jobs, and several hundred have received prison sentences for their religious beliefs, most recently for participating in study circles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Bahá'í cemeteries have been desecrated and property has been seized and occasionally demolished, including the House of Mírzá Buzurg, Bahá'u'lláh's father.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The House of the Báb in <a href="/wiki/Shiraz,_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiraz, Iran">Shiraz</a>, one of three sites to which Bahá'ís perform pilgrimage, has been destroyed twice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolter200575–114-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENetherlands_Institute_of_Human_Rights8_March_2006_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENetherlands_Institute_of_Human_Rights8_March_2006-137">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service2005_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service2005-138">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
In May 2018, the Iranian authorities expelled a young woman student from university of <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a> because she was Bahá'í.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018, two more Bahá'í students were expelled  from universities in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Zanjan,_Iran" title="Zanjan, Iran">Zanjan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilan_Province" title="Gilan Province">Gilan</a> because of their religion.
</p><p>According to a US panel, attacks on Bahá'ís in Iran increased under <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a>'s presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN16_May_2008_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN16_May_2008-140">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan8_December_2009_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan8_December_2009-141">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">United Nations Commission on Human Rights</a> revealed an October 2005 confidential letter from Command Headquarters of the Armed Forces of Iran ordering its members to identify Bahá'ís and to monitor their activities. Due to these actions, the <a href="/wiki/Special_Rapporteur_(UN)" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Rapporteur (UN)">Special Rapporteur</a> of the United Nations Commission on Human Rights stated on 20 March 2006, that she "also expresses concern that the information gained as a result of such monitoring will be used as a basis for the increased persecution of, and discrimination against, members of the Bahá'í faith, in violation of international standards. The Special Rapporteur is concerned that this latest development indicates that the situation with regard to religious minorities in Iran is, in fact, deteriorating."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJahangir2006_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJahangir2006-142">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 May 2008, members of an informal body known as the "Friends" that oversaw the needs of the Bahá'í community in Iran were arrested and taken to <a href="/wiki/Evin_prison" class="mw-redirect" title="Evin prison">Evin prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN16_May_2008_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN16_May_2008-140">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center15_May_2008_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center15_May_2008-143">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>  The Friends court case has been postponed several times, but was finally underway on 12 January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN12_January_2010_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN12_January_2010-144">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Other observers were not allowed in the court. Even the defence lawyers, who for two years have had minimal access to the defendants, had difficulty entering the courtroom. The chairman of the U.S. Commission on International Religious Freedom said that it seems that the government has already predetermined the outcome of the case and is violating international human rights law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN12_January_2010_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN12_January_2010-144">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Further sessions were held on 7 February 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWashington_TV2010_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWashington_TV2010-145">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> 12 April 2010<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDjavadi8_April_2010_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDjavadi8_April_2010-146">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and 12 June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERadio_Free_Europe3_June_2010_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERadio_Free_Europe3_June_2010-147">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> On 11 August 2010 it became known that the court sentence was 20 years imprisonment for each of the seven prisoners<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESiegal2010_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESiegal2010-148">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> which was later reduced to ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN16_September_2010_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN16_September_2010-149">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> After the sentence, they were transferred to <a href="/wiki/Gohardasht_prison" class="mw-redirect" title="Gohardasht prison">Gohardasht prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAFP16_February_2011_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAFP16_February_2011-150">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In March 2011 the sentences were reinstated to the original 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAFP31_March_2011_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAFP31_March_2011-151">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> On 3 January 2010, Iranian authorities detained ten more members of the Baha'i minority, reportedly including Leva Khanjani, granddaughter of Jamaloddin Khanjani, one of seven Baha'i leaders jailed since 2008 and in February, they arrested his son, Niki Khanjani.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Jerusalem_Post14_February_2010_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Jerusalem_Post14_February_2010-152">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Iranian government claims that the Bahá'í Faith is not a religion, but is instead a political organization, and hence refuses to recognize it as a minority religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKravetz1982237_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKravetz1982237-153">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> However, the government has never produced convincing evidence supporting its characterization of the Bahá'í community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center20085_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center20085-154">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Also, the government's statements that Bahá'ís who recanted their religion would have their rights restored, attest to the fact that Bahá'ís are persecuted solely for their religious affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center20079_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center20079-155">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The Iranian government also accuses the Bahá'í Faith of being associated with <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionism</a> because the Bahá'í World Centre is located in Haifa, Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007Statement_of_the_Embassy_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran,_Buenos_Aires,_26_September_1979_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIran_Human_Rights_Documentation_Center2007Statement_of_the_Embassy_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran,_Buenos_Aires,_26_September_1979-156">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> These accusations against the Bahá'ís have no basis in historical fact,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper199320_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper199320-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpsonShubart1995223_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpsonShubart1995223-136">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETavakoli-Targhi2008200_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETavakoli-Targhi2008200-158">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> and the accusations are used by the Iranian government to use the Bahá'ís as "scapegoats".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreedman26_June_2009_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreedman26_June_2009-159">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In fact it was the Iranian leader Naser al-Din Shah Qajar who banished Bahá'u'lláh from Iran to the Ottoman Empire and Bahá'u'lláh was later exiled by the Ottoman Sultan, at the behest of the Iranian Shah, to territories further away from Iran and finally to <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> in Syria, which only a century later was incorporated into the state of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen200427–29_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen200427–29-160">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1920s Egypt's religious Tribunal recognized the Baha'i Faith as a new, independent religion, totally separate from Islam, due to the nature of the 'laws, principles and beliefs' of the Baha'is.  At the same time the Tribunal condemned "in most unequivocal and emphatic language the followers of Baha'u'llah as the believers in heresy, offensive and injurious to Islam, and wholly incompatible with the accepted doctrines and practice of its orthodox adherents."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bahá'í institutions and community activities have been illegal under Egyptian law since 1960. All Bahá'í community properties, including Bahá'í centers, libraries, and cemeteries, have been confiscated by the government and <a href="/wiki/Fatwa" title="Fatwa">fatwas</a> have been issued charging Bahá'ís with <a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">apostasy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013&#91;https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222287_Egypt&#93;_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Religious_Freedom_Report2013[https2009-2017stategovjdrlrlsirfreligiousfreedomindexhtmyear2013dlid222287_Egypt]-162">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_identification_card_controversy" title="Egyptian identification card controversy">Egyptian identification card controversy</a> began in the 1990s when the government modernized the electronic processing of <a href="/wiki/Identity_documents" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity documents">identity documents</a>, which introduced a de facto requirement that documents must list the person's religion as Muslim, Christian, or Jewish (the only three religions officially recognized by the government). Consequently, Bahá'ís were unable to obtain government identification documents (such as national identification cards, birth certificates, death certificates, marriage or divorce certificates, or passports) necessary to exercise their rights in their country unless they lied about their religion, which conflicts with Bahá'í religious principle. Without documents, they could not be employed, educated, treated in hospitals, travel outside of the country, or vote, among other hardships.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBigelow16_November_2005_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBigelow16_November_2005-163">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Following a protracted legal process culminating in a court ruling favorable to the Bahá'ís, the interior minister of Egypt released a decree on 14 April 2009, amending the law to allow Egyptians who are not Muslim, Christian, or Jewish to obtain identification documents that list a dash in place of one of the three recognized religions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service17_April_2009_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service17_April_2009-164">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The first identification cards were issued to two Bahá'ís under the new decree on 8 August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service14_August_2009_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBahá&#39;í_World_News_Service14_August_2009-165">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Outline of the Bahá&#39;í Faith">Outline of the Bahá'í Faith</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bahá'ís prefer the orthographies <i>Bahá'í</i>, <i>Bahá'ís</i>, <i>the Báb</i>, <i>Bahá'u'lláh</i>, and <i>`Abdu'l-Bahá </i>, using a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_orthography" title="Bahá&#39;í orthography">particular transcription</a> of the Arabic and Persian in publications. "Bahai", "Bahais", "Baha'i", "the Bab", "Bahaullah" and "Baha'u'llah" are often used when <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a> are unavailable.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For an annotated compilation of excerpts from the Bahá'í writings regarding the principle of International or Universal Auxiliary Language, see The Greatest Instrument for Promoting Harmony and Civilization: Excerpts from the Bahá'í Writings and Related Sources on the Question of an International Auxiliary Language. Oxford: George Ronald. 2015. <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886058088">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-registration a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-gray-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-red-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-085398-591-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-085398-591-4">978-085398-591-4</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Obedience to government is not applicable when submission to law amounts to a denial of Faith. See for example: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bahaistudies.net/nonpolitical.html">Political Non-involvement and Obedience to Government&#160;– A compilation of some of the Messages of the Guardian and the Universal House of Justice</a> (compiled by Dr. Peter J. Khan)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">All Ridván messages can be found at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bahai.org/library/authoritative-texts/the-universal-house-of-justice/messages">Bahai.org</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bahaiprayers.net/Ridvan">Bahaiprayers.net/Ridvan</a> (multi-lingual).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In line with this is the thinking that the government encouraged the campaign to distract attention from more serious problems, including acute economic difficulties. Beyond this lay the difficulty which the regime faced in harnessing the nationalist movement that had supported Musaddiq.(<a href="#CITEREFAkhavi1980">Akhavi 1980</a>, pp.&#160;76–78)</span>
</li>
</ol></div>
